A description will be specifically giver, with respect to an organic dye material in the present embodiment having characteristics described in "5-1) Description of characteristics relating to "L-H" recording film in the present embodiment", the present embodiment meeting a condition shown in "5-2,

Characteristics of optical absorption spectra relating to "L-H" recording film" in the present embodiment". The thickness of the recording layer 3-2 meets the conditions shown in formulas (3), (4), (27), and (28), and is formed by spinner coating (spin coating). For comparison, a description will be given by way of example. A crystal of a "salt" is assembled by "ion coupling" between positively charged "sodium ions" and negatively charged "chloride ions". Similarly, in polymers as well, there is a case in which a plurality of polymers are combined with each other in the form close to "ion coupling", forming configuring an organic dye material. The organic dye recording film 3-2 in the present embodiment is composed of a positively charged "cation portion" and a negatively charged "anion portion". In particular, the above recording film is technically featured in that: coupling stability is improved by utilizing a "dye" having chromogenic characteristics for the positively charged "cation portion" and utilizing an organic metal complex for the negatively charged "anion portion"; and there is met a condition that "8] an electron structure in a chromogenic area is stabilized, and structural decomposition relevant to ultraviolet ray or reproduction light irradiation hardly occurs" shewn in "3-2-B] Basic feature common to organic dye recording material in the present embodiment". Specifically, in

the present embodiment, an "azo metal complex" whose general structural formula is shown in FIG. 3 is utilized as an organic metal complex. In the present embodiment which comprises a combination of an anion portion and a cation portion, cobalt or nickel is used as a center metal M of this azo metal complex, thereby enhancing optical stability. There may be used: scandium, yttrium, titanium, zirconium, hafnium, vanadium, niobium, tantalum, chrome, molybdenum, tungsten, manganese, technetium, rhenium, iron, ruthenium, osmium, rhodium, iridium, palladium, platinum, copper, silver, gold, zinc, cadmium, or mercury and the like without being limited thereto. In the present embodiment, as a dye used for the cation portion, there is used any of a cyanine dye whose general structural formula is shown in FIG. 27; a styril dye whose general structural formula is shown in FIG. 28; and a monomethine cyanine dye whose general structural formula is shown in FIG. 29.
Although an azo metal complex is used for the anion portion in the present embodiment, a formazane metal complex whose general structural formula is shown in FIG. 30 may be used without being limited thereto, for example. The organic dye recording material comprising the anion portion and cation portion is first powdered. In the case of forming the recording layer 3-2, the powdered organic dye receding material

is dissolved in organic solvent, and spin coating is carried out on the transparent substrate 2-2. At this time, the organic solvent to be used includes: a fluorine alcohol based TFP (tetrafluoro propanol) or pentane; hexane; cyclohexane; petroleum ether; ether or analogous, nitrile or analogous, and any of a nitro compound or sulfur-containing compound or a combination thereof.
5-4) Using "copper" as azo metal complex + center metal
FIGS. 65 and 66 each show an example of a light spectrum change before and after recording (forming a recording mark) in an "H-L" recording film and an "L-H" recording film using an optical characteristic change according to the present embodiment as a principle of recording. A wavelength of ^max write before recording (in an unrecorded area) is defined as A,bmax write; a half value width of a light absorption spectrum (b) around this Xmax write (a width of a wavelength area meeting a range of "A > 0.5" when the absorbance A at ^bmax write is "1") is defined as Was; and a wavelength °f 'Wax write of a light absorption spectrum (a) after recorded (in a recording mark) is defined as A,amax write- The recording film 3-2 having the characteristics shown in FIGS. 65 and 66 utilizes a "change of an electron structure (electron orbit) relevant to elements which contribute to a chromogenic

phenomenon and a "molecular structure change in molecules" from among the principles of recording shown in [a] of "3-2-B] Basic characteristics common to organic dye recording material in the invention". If there occurs a "change of an electron structure (electron orbit) relevant to electrons which contribute to a chromogenic phenomenon", for example, the dimensions or structure of the light emitting area 8 as shown in FIG. 3 changes. For example, if dimensions of the light emitting area 8 change., the resonant absorption wavelength of the local electrons also changes, and thus, the maximum absorption wavelength of light absorption spectra changes from A,bmax write to max write- Similarly, if a "molecular structure change in molecules" occurs, a structure of the light emitting area 8 also changes, and thus, the maximum absorption wavelength of the light absorption spectra also changes. When a change amount of the maximum absorption wavelength is defined as AXmax, the following relationship is established:
A-max write max write I (49) When the maximum absorption wavelength of the light absorption spectra thus changes, the half value width Was of the light absorption spectra also changes concurrently. A description will be given with respect to an effect on a reproduction signal obtained from a recording mark position when the maximum absorption

wavelength of the light absorption spectra and the half" value width Was of the light absorption spectra have thus changed at the same time. The light absorption spectra in a pre-recording/unrecorded area are represented as (b) in FIG. 65 (FIG. 66), and thus, the absorbance with a reproduction light beam having 405 nm is obtained as Ah4Q5 (A1405)• If only the maximum absorption wavelength changes to A,amax write as optical spectra after recorded (in recording mark) and a change of the half value width Was has not occurred, the light absorption spectra are theoretically obtained as shown in (c) of FIG. 65 (FIG. 66). Then, the absorbance with a reproduction light beam having 405 nm changes to A*405- However, in actuality, the half value width changes, and the absorbance after recorded (in recording mark) is obtained as A14Q5 (Ah405)• A change amount I £.1405 - Ah405l of the absorbance before and after recorded is proportional to a reproduction signal amplitude value. Thus, in the example shown in FIG. 65 (FIG. 66), the maximum absorption wavelength change and the half width value change work as an offset action relevant to an increase of the reproduction signal amplitude. Therefore, there occurs a problem that a C/N ratio of a reproduction signal is impaired. A first application example of the present embodiment for solving the above problem is featured in that the characteristics of the recording layer 3-2 is set

(film-designed) so that a maximum absorption wavelength change and a half value width change work relevant to an increase of the reproduction signal amplitude in a synergetic manner. That is, as is easily predicted from the change shown in FIG. 65 (FIG. 66), the characteristics of the recording layer 3-2 is set (film-designed) so that a change occurs in a direction in which a half value width widens independent of a moving direction of A.amax write after recorded relevant to Xbmax write before recorded in the "H-L" recording film or in a direction in which the half value width narrows independent of a moving direction of A,amax write after recorded relevant to A,bmax write before recorded in the "L-H" recording film.
Now, a second application example in the present embodiment will be described here. As described previously, there is a case in which the C/N ratio of tne reproduction signal is lowered by offsetting a difference between AhQ5 and A14Q5 due to the maximum absorption wavelength change and the change of the half value width Was. Further, in the above first application example or the embodiment shown in FIG. 65 or FIG. 66, the maximum absorption wavelength change and the half value width Was of the light absorption spectra change at the same time, a value of the absorbance "A" after recorded (in recording mark) is affected by both of the maximum absorption wavelength

change amount AXmax and the half value width change amount. When the write-once type information storage medium 12 has been mass-produced, it is difficult to precisely control values of both of the maximum absorption wavelength change amount AXmax and the half value width change amount. Thus, when the information is recorded in the mass-produced write-once type information storage medium 12 has been recorded, a fluctuation of the reproduction signal amplitude increases. Then, the reliability of the reproduction signal is lowered when the signal has been reproduced by the information reproducing apparatus shown in FIGi. 11. In contrast, the second application example in the present embodiment is featured in that a material of which the maximum absorption wavelength does not change between before and after recorded (between the recording mark and the unrecorded area) . Therefore, a fluctuation of values of the absorbance "A" after recorded (in recording mark) is suppressed and a fluctuation between the individuals of the reproduction signal amplitude from the above value fluctuation is reduced, whereby the reliability of the reproduction signal has been improved. In this second application example, the maximum absorption wavelength does not; change between before and after recording (in recording mark and in unrecorded area), and the value of the absorbance "A" is determined depending on only

the spread of the light absorption spectra before and after recording (in recording mark and in unrecorded area). When a large number of write-once type information storage mediums 12 have been mass-produced, it is sufficient if only the spread of the light absorption spectra before and after recorded (in recording mark and in unrecorded area) is controlled, and thus, a fluctuation in characteristics between mediums can be reduced. Even if a contrivance is made so that a maximum absorption wavelength before and after recording (in recording mark and in unrecorded area) does not change, strictly, it is difficult to completely match the values of bmax write each other, as shown in FIG. 68. The half value width Was of the light absorption spectra around A,bmax write shown in FIG. 65 or 66 is often included in the range of 100 rim to 200 nm in a general organic dye recording material. Therefore, if the value of the maximum absorption wavelength change amount AX,max exceeds 100 nm, it is possible to easily predict from FIG. 65 or 66 that there occurs a large difference between the absorbance Ah405 (^1495) obtained from the characteristics of item (b) and the absorption A*4Q5 obtained from the characteristics of item (c). Accordingly, the fact that "the maximum absorption wavelength does not change" as the second application example mans that the following condition is met:

^ 100 nm (50)
Further, when a condition that the maximum absorption wavelength change amount AA.max is 1/3 of the value obtained by formula (50), i.e.,
AXmax a difference between the absorbance Ah^QS (A14Q5) obtained from the characteristics of item (b) and the absorption A*405 obtained from the characteristics of item (c) is very small, and a fluctuation in reproduction signal characteristics between the mediums can be reduced.
FIG. 68 shows the "L-H" recording film characteristics, which meet formula (50) or formula (51). The light absorption spectra before recorded (in unrecorded area) are obtained as wide spectra as shown in the characteristic (b) of FIG. 68, and the absorbance Ah4Q5 at a reproduction wavelength of 405 nm is obtained as a sufficient small value. The absorbance Ah^Q5 after recorded (in recording mark) narrows in width as shown in the characteristic (a) of FIG. 68, and the absorbance A14Q5 at a reproduction wavelength of 405 nm rises.
In order to meet formula (50) or formula (51), the present embodiment utilizes an "orientation change in molecules" in item [a] of "3-2-B] Basic characteristics common to organic dye recording material in the invention" as a principle of recording. In the azo

metal complex shown in FIG. 3, a plurality of benzene nucleus rings are located on the same plane because the benzene nucleus rings are radically coupled with each other. That is, in FIG. 3, four benzene nuclear rings which exist more upwardly than the center metal M forms an U (up-side) plane which the benzene nucleus group produced; and four benzene nuclear rings which exist more downwardly than the center metal M forms a D (down-side) plane which the benzene nucleus group produced.
A mutually parallel relationship is always maintained between the above U plane and D plane in any case (irrespective of whether pre-recording or post-recording may be). Side chain groups of Rl and R3 are arranged in a form orthogonal to the above U plane and D plane. Ion coupling is carried out between the center metal atom M and the oxygen atom 0, and a plane formed by a line segment for connecting 0-M-O is located in parallel to the above U plane and D plane. The light emitting area 8 surrounded in a round area shown in FIG. 3 has such a three-dimensional structure. For further description, a direction oriented from a direction of R4 to a direction of R5 in the U plane is tentatively defined as a "Yu direction", and a direction oriented from a direction of R4 to a direction of R5 in the D plane is defined as a "Yd direction". Orientation coupling is carried out

«.
between a nitrogen atom N included in the U plane or D plane and the center metal atom M sandwiched between these two planes so that a position of the nitrogen atom N around the center metal atom M can be rotated. That is, a structure is provided such that the Yd direction can be rotated with respect to the Yu direction while a mutually parallel relationship is maintained between the above U plane and D plane. In the azo metal complex shown in FIG. 3, the Yu direction and Yd direction can be parallel to each other, as shown in FIG. 67A (the orientations can be made identical or opposite to each other as shown in FIG. 67A); and the Yu direction and Yd direction can be in a skew position relationship as shown in FIG. 67B. Of course, an arbitrary angle relationship between FIGS. 67A and 67B can be also established. As described previously, the side chain groups of Rl and R3 are arranged in a form orthogonal to the above U plane and D plane. Thus, in the structure of FIG. 67A, collision is likely to occur between the side chain group of Rl or R3 and another side chain group of R4 or the like. Therefore, as shown in FIG. 67B, a time point at which the Yu direction and Yd direction are in a skew position relationship (when the U plane is seen from far above, the Yu direction and Yd direction are seen as if it were orthogonal to each other) is the most stable in a structural point of view. The light

absorption wavelength in the light emitting area 8 when the state shown in FIG. 67B is established coincides with a value of Xamax write = ^bmax write shown in FIG. 68. If the relationship between the Yu direction and Yd direction deviates from the state shown in FIG. 67B, the electron structure in the light emitting area 8 and the local distance of light absorption electrons (the size of local area) slightly change, and the light absorption wavelength deviates from the value
of ^amax write = ^bmax write- BY means of spinner coating, a relationship between the above Yu direction and Yd direction is arbitrarily oriented in the recording layer 3-2 (in unrecorded state) immediately after formed on the transparent substrate 2-2. Therefore, the distribution width of light absorption spectra widens as shown in characteristic (b) of FIG. 68. In order to form a recording mark, when a temperature in the recording layer 3-2 is locally risen, a molecular orientation moves because of a high temperature, and finally, an almost stable state shown in FIG. 6"?B is established in a structural point of view. Then, the electron structures in the light emitting area 8 coincide with each other anywhere in the recording mark, and the current spectra changes to narrow light absorption spectra in width, as shown in characteristic (a) of FIG. 68. As a result, the absorbance at a reproduction wavelength (for example,

405 nm) changes from A14Q5 to
A description will be made with respect another advantageous effect of using the light emitting area 8 in an azo metal complex. A dye is utilized for a cation portion in the case of utilizing a combination of the anion portion and the cation portion described previously. Although the chromogenic area in each of the dyes shown in FIGS. 27 to 29 occupies a portion in each of the dye structures, a relative occupying capacitance of the chromogenic area in the recording layer 3-2 is decreased by combining this area with an anion portion which does not contribute to the chromogenic area. Therefore, a light absorption sectional area is relatively lowered, and a molar molecule light absorption coefficient is lowered. As a result, a value of the absorbance at a position of A.max write shown in FIG. 25 is reduced, and recording sensitivity is lowered. In contrast, in the case of utilizing the chromogenic characteristics at the periphery of the center metal of an azo metal complex itself described here, the azo metal complex itself emits light, and thus, there does not exist a redundant portion which does not contribute to a chromogenic area such as the anion portion described previously. Therefore, there is no unnecessary factor that the relative occupying capacitance of the chromogenic area decreases. Further, as shown in FIG. 3, the occupying

capacitance of the light emitting area 8 in the azo metal complex is wide, and thus, the light absorption sectional area increases, and a value of the molar molecule light absorption coefficient rises. As a result, there is provided advantageous effect that the value of the absorbance at a position of ^max write shown in FIG. 25 increases, and the recording sensitivity is improved.
The present embodiment is featured in that the structural stability of the chromogenic area .has been achieved by optimizing the center metal of the azo metal complex as a specific method for "5] stabilizing an electron structure in a chromogenic area so that structural decomposition relevant to ultraviolet ray or reproduction light irradiation hardly occurs" described in "3-2-Bj Basic characteristics common to organic dye recording material in the invention".
It is known that metal ions have their unique ionization tendency. These metal atoms are arranged in stronger order of ionization tendency, i.e., Na > Mg > Al > Zn > Fe > Ni > Cu > Hg > Ag > Au. The ionization tendency of the metal atoms represents "nature of metal radiating electrons to form positive ions".
After a variety of metal atoms has been incorporated as the center metal of the azo metal complex having the structure shown in FIG. 3, where reproduction stability (stability of chromogenic

characteristics when a light beam in the vicinity of 405 nm is repeatedly irradiated with reproduction power) is repeatedly checked, it has been found that the metal atoms with high ionization tendency radiates electrons more remarkably and are easily decoupled; and the light emitting area 8 is easily destroyed. As a result of a number of tests, in order to ensure structural stabilization of the chromogenic area, it has been found desirable to use a metal material (Ni, Cu, Hg, Ag, Au) after nickel (Ni) as the center metal. Further, from the viewpoint of "structural stability of high chromogenic area", "low price", and "use safety", it is the most desirable to use copper (Cu) as the center metal as the present embodiment. In the present embodiment, any of CH3, CxHy, H, Cl, F, N02, S02, and S02NHCH3 is used as Rl, R2, R3, R4, or R5 which is a side chair, shown in FIG. 3.
Now, a description will be given with respect to a method for forming an organic dye recording material having a molecular structure shown in FIG. 3 as the recording layer 3-2 on a transparent substrate 2-2. The powdered organic dye recording material of 1.49 g is dissolved in 100 nm of TFP (tetrafluoro propanol) which is a fluorine alcohol based solvent. The above numeric value denotes that 1.4 wt% is obtained as a mixture ratio, and an actual use amount changes depending on a manufacture amount of the write-once

type information storage medium. It is desirable that the mixture ratio ranges from 1.2 wt% to 1.5 wt%. As a solvent, it is conditionally mandatory that a surface of the transparent substrate 2-2 made of a polycarbonate resin is not dissolved, and the above described alcohol based solvent is used. Because the above TFP (tetrafluoro propanol) has polarity, the solubility of the powdered organic dye recording material is improved. While the transparent substrate 2-2 on a spindle motor is rotated, the organic dye recording material dissolved in the solvent is applied to the center part of the transparent substrate 2-2 until the solvent has evaporated after the material has been spread by utilizing a centrifugal force, and then, the recording layer 3-2 is compressed in accordance with a baking process for increasing the entire temperature.
5-5) Azo metal complex whose center metal is ion-bonded with four oxygen atoms
In the case of a structure in which two oxygen ions are ion-bonded with a center metal shown in FIG. 5, in principle of operation, recording is carried out by an arrangement angle between a U plane and a D plane produced by a benzene nucleus group, as shcv.-n in FIGS. 67A and 67B.
As described above, copper or the like is used as a material for the center metal M, and thereby

molecules are strongly bonded with each other, and molecular destruction caused by ultraviolet irradiation hardly occurs. Thus, long-term stability is ensured as shown in FIGS. 67A and 67B. However, in the case where only two oxygen atoms are ion-bonded with the center metal M, rotation is likely to occur between the U plane and the D plane produced by the benzene nucleus group, as shown in FIGS. 67A and 67B. Thus, by carrying out repetition reproduction, an unrecorded area shown in FIG. 67A gradually changes to allocation after recording, as shown in FIG. 67B. Therefore, there occurs a phenomenon that a recorded signal is degraded.
As an application example for solving the above problem, the present embodiment employs a structure of four oxygen atoms to be ion-bonded with the center metal, as shown in FIGS. 98A and 98B. In FIGS. 58A and 98B, there is used cobalt Co having a trivalent ion as a center metal. An application example is not limited thereto, and iron, rare earth metals, aluminum, or yttrium can be used as those having a trivalent center metal ion instead of cobalt. By using the trivalent center metal ion in this way, as shown in FIGS. 98A and 98B, ion bonding with four oxygen atoms can be achieved at the periphery of the center metal ion. The four oxygen atoms are thus arranged at symmetrical pcsitions at the periphery of the center metal cobalt ion,

nitrogen-containing organic compound, triethyl amine whose structural formula is shown in FIG. 99A is employed in the present embodiment. Its three-dimensional structural view is shown in FIG. 99B. In the present embodiment, triethyl amine is used as a polymer having a positive charge. However, without being limited thereto, in another embodiment, there can be used: an aminium salt based compound; an arr.ime compound; an animothiol nickel complex based compound; an inmonium based compound; a cyanine based compound; an iminium based compound; a dithiol nickel complex compound; or alternatively, a cation such as an ammonium ion or a tetraalkyl ammonium ion. In addition, as the above amine compound, there can be used: tripropyl amine; tributyl amine; secondary butyl amine; tertiary butyl amine; hexyl amine; N-methyl cyclohexyl amine; benzyl amine; N, N-diisopropyl ethyl amine, or 2, 6-xylidine or the like. Further, according to the present embodiment, a polymer having a positive charge is set to be equal to or smaller than a value of a specific molecular weight. While a molecular weight of triethyl amine shown in FIG. 99A is 118, if the molecular weight of this polymer having a positive cnarge exceeds 1200, solubility in organic solvent when a recording layer is formed is impaired, making it difficult to form a stable recording film. Therefore, the molecular weight of the polymer having a

positive charge in the present embodiment is set to be 1200 or less. Further, from a variety of tests, it has been found that a desirable condition in which solubility in solvent is high is that a molecular weight is 250 or less.
The present embodiment utilizes an organic polymer as a substance having a positive charge for electrically neutralizing an organic metal complex having a negative charge. However, in the present embodiment, a metal ion such as a sodium ion, for example, can be used without being limited thereto.
FIG. 100A shows a three-dimensionally combined structural view formed by combining structural views of the azo metal complex shown in FIGS. 98A and 98B and triethyl amine shown in FIGS. 99A and 99B. Specifically, a hydrogen atom allocated at a position at which N+ in triethyl amine is proximal to a position proximal to center metal cobalt, the hydrogen atom being proximal to a nitrogen ion in triethyl amine, is allocated in the form such that it is partially inserted between cobalt and the coloring area 8. FIG. 100B shows a schematic view relevant to the structural view shown in FIG. 100A.
A principle of coloring in the coloring area 8 in the azo metal complex shown in FIGS. 98A and 98B will be described below. FIG. 101A shows a part of the structural formula shown in FIG. 98A, and FIG. 101B

shows a re-electron orbit in the case where no center metal cobalt exists. Essentially, when a negative ion (cobalt atom having a charge) approaches the vicinity where an electron orbit should be arranged vertically evenly, the electron orbit is distorted, as shown in FIG. 1018, under the influence of the center metal ion. As a result, a coloring action occurs. In FIG. 101B, a description is given with respect to an electron orbit by repulsion caused by approaching of the negative charge for the sake of simplification. In actuality, a mixture orbit between a d-orbit which is a part of the metal atoms and the above 7i-orbit is produced, and coloring is carried out. With respect to an electron distribution of Tt-electrons, as shown in FIG. 101C, the vicinity of each atom is the highest in electron distribution density, and is low in electron distribution density between atoms. As shown in FIG. 102, if a certain force acts with a distance between original atoms, and then, a distance between atoms is reduced, and the localization range of K-electrcns becomes narrow as shown in FIG. 102 (a). As a result, a wavelength of absorption light is reduced. In contrast, as shown in FIG. 102 (b), conversely, when a distance between atoms increases, the localization range of 7t-electrons becomes wider, and the wavelength of absorption light becomes long. In the case of using the above-described organic

dye based recording material, an "orientation or arrangement change in molecules (or between molecules) is utilized from a principle of recording described in "3-2-B] Basic characteristics common to organic dye recording materials in the present embodiment" in "3-2) Description of basic characteristics common to organic dye recording film in the present embodiment".
That, is, in the case of using a combination of the azo metal complex and triethyl amine according to the present embodiment, combined molecules are arranged and allocated before recording. As a result, as shown in FIG. 103A, a coagulation force 1001 acts in a vertical direction. In addition, at the time of recording, the arrangement of molecules greatly moves under the influences of thermal energy. After recording, as shown in FIG. 103B, random arrangement occurs. As a result, the coagulation force weakens as compared with FIG. 103A. In addition, as shown in FIG. 98B, the four oxygen atoms ion-bonded with the center metal is bonded with one carbon atom in a benzene nucleus in the coloring area 8. Thus, as shown in FIG. 103A, when the coagulation force 1001 acts, the oxygen atom pushes up the benzene nucleus. As shown in FIG. 104, a distance between atoms at the periphery of the carbon atorr. bonded with the pushed up oxygen atom increases. Conversely, a distance between atoms in carbon atoms in the benzene nucleus distant from the oxygen atoms is

reduced. As a result, the range of absorption wavelength widens, and the width of light absorption spectra widens (reference should be made to "half value width Was before recording" shown in FIG. 106). Further, as shown in FIG. 99B, three carbon atoms and one hydrogen atom surrounding the nitrogen ion in triethyl amine have a regular tetrahedron, and is formed in a wedge shape relevant to the azo metal complex. Thus, the coagulation force acts, and thereby, as shown in FIG. 105, triethyl amine pushes out the nitrogen atom or carbon atom from the inside of the coloring area 8. As a result, a distance between carbon atoms, a distance between a nitrogen atom and a carbon atom, or a distance between nitrogen atoms is reduced, and the maximum absorption wavelength ?tbmax write i-3 reduced. As a result, as shown in FIG. 106 (b', the half value width Was of the absorption spectra before recording is wide, and the value of the maximum absorption wavelength A,bmax Write ^s short. On the other hand, as shown in FIG. 103B, when the coagulation force is weakened by random allocation of molecules after recording, the above pushing force weakens. As a result, a distance between atoms is restored to its original state. Thus, as shown in FIG. 106 (a), after recording, the maximum absorption wavelength ^amax write is shifted to the long wavelength side, as compared with Xbmax write'the half value width Was

becomes narrow. As a result, the light absorbance is lowered from A14Q5 to An405 at a position of 405 nm of reproduction light, and a light reflectivity increases. As has been described above, an organic dye recording material is composed of a combination of an organic metal complex and a nitrogen-containing organic compound, the metal complex being formed by ion bonding between a trivalent center metal ion and four oxygen atoms. As shown in FIGS. 103A and 103B, recording is carried out by a change in arrangement between molecules, and there are provided "L-H" recording characteristics. As described previously, in the case where a "change of orientation or arrangement in molecules or between molecules" occurs, a change rate in maximum absorption wavelength caused by a change in distance between atoms is comparatively small. Thus, as has been described in formula (50) or formula (51) above, a value of a change of the maximum absorption wavelength, AXmax, is small. Thus, a characteristic dispersion between media before and after recording when a large number of write-once type information storage mediums 12 have been mass-produced can be reduced, and the performance stability at the time of mass-production can be ensured. Therefore, in the present embodiment, a contrivance is made to meet a condition of AXmax
becomes narrow. As a result, the light absorbance is lowered from AlQS to AhQS at a position of 405 nm of reproduction light, and a light reflectivity increases. Another application example relevant to a principle of recording shown in FIGS. 103A and 103B will be described below.
Molecules are arranged in order before recording, and are arranged in random after recording as shown in FIGS. 103A and 103B. Conversely, in another application example, a principle of recording is employed such that random arrangement is provided before recording, and normal arrangement is provided after recording. In order to enable this, a solvent having polarity is utilized when forming a recording layer using an organic dye based recording material. As a specific solvent having polarity, in the present embodiment, a fluorine alcohol is used. As an example of fluorine alcohol, FIG. 107A shows a structural formula of tetra fluoro propanol (TFP).
As shown in FIG. 107A, in tetra fluoro propanol, three carbon atoms produces a main chain, fluorine atoms are arranged at its periphery, and an OH group is arranged at its terminal. Then, electron eccentricity occurs betv;een the OH group and the carbon atoms adjacent thereto, and, as shown in FIG. 107A, polarization of a negative charge and a positive charge occurs wit:: the OH group side and the carbon side adjacent thereto, respectively. A schematic view of this polarization is shown in FIG. 107B. The azo metal

t
complex and triethyl amine molecules having a structure shown in FIG. 100A are dissolved in a tetra flucro propanol solvent shown in FIG. 107A, and is coated on a transparent substrate, thereby forming a recording layer. At this time, because tetra fluoro propanol has polarization, a portion at which the center metal (cobalt) in the azo metal complex and the nitrogen ion in triethyl amine are arranged and the tetra fluoro propanol are pulled each other. As a result, there occurs a phenomenon that tetra fluoro propanol v.-hich is an organic solvent partially remains immediately after forming the recording layer. As a result, tetra fluoro propanol which remains without being volatilized inhibits molecular arrangement, and the arrangement of organic dye molecules is randomized, as shown ir. FIG. 108A, In FIG. 108A, a portion expressed by the schematic view shown in FIG. 107B shows tetra fluoro propanol molecules which remain without being volatilized. At the time of recording, because a high temperature is achieved, the remaining organic solvent molecules completely volatilizes, and thus a factor of inhibitinq arrangement is dissolved. As a result, after recording, as shown in FIG. 108B, organic dye molecules are arranged each other. A description will be given below with respect to an effect of molecular arrangement shown in FIGS. 108A and 108B on a reproduction signal.

As shown in FIG. 108A, at a portion at which tetra fluoro propanol which is an organic solvent molecule has remained, a distance between cobalt in the azo metal complex and a nitrogen ion in triethyl amine is increased under the influence of the above remaining molecule. As shown in FIG. 109A, an effect of only a cobalt ion appears against covalent bonding in the coloring area 8. In contrast, where an organic solvent molecule having polarization volatilizes, the nitrogen ion in triethyl amine approaches the center metal in the azo metal complex (FIG. 109B). Thus, charge based neutralization occurs due to a charge of a nitrogen ion, and a electron orbit extends downwardly as shown in FIG. 109C. Accordingly, the maximum absorption wavelength becomes long. As a result, is greater than write' FIG. 106; "he light, absorbance obtained when reproduction is carried out with reproduction light at 405 nm changes from Al^os to An405' and the change appears as a reproduction signal. However, as shown in FIG. 109C, a change rate of the n-electron orbit due to charge based neutralization of nitrogen ions is very small, and thus, wavelength difference AXmax between A.amax write and A.bmax Write snown in FIG. 106 is small, and the above-described formula (50) or (51) is met. Therefore, a specific dispersion between mediums before and after recording where a large number of write-once

type information storage mediums 12 have been mass-produced is reduced, and stable mass-production can be carried out.
5-6) Mixture structure of a plurality of organic dye based recording materials
ft description has been given with respect zo an organic dye based recording material composed by-electrostatic linking of a negatively charged organic metal complex and a positively charged nitrogen-containing organic compound as an embodiment of the above-described section "5-5) azo metal complex in which a center metal is ion-bonded with four oxygen atoms". According to the present application example, a description will be given with respect to an example of forming a recording layer by mixing an organic dye based recording material or the like using "5-3.• Anion portion: azo metal complex + cation portion : dye" with respect to an organic dye based recording material composed of the above nitrogen-containing organic compound and organic metal complex. FIG. 110A shows a structural view of a cyanine dye used as a caticr. port] on. In addition, FIG. HOB shows a three-dimensionally combined structure where an azo metal complex of an organic metal complex is used as ar. anion portion and a cyanine dye is combined as a dye of a cation portion. As shown in FIG. 100B, in the case of using triethyl amine, a molecule weight of triethyl

amine is small, and thus, the size of triethyl amine is much smaller than that of the azo metal complex. In comparison, as shown in FIG. HOB, a cyanine dye is very large in molecular weight, and thus, is bonded with the azo metal complex in such a manner that the cyanine dye overreaches the limit in a vertical direction. FIG. HOC shows a schematic view of "he above-described three-dimensionally combined structure. The center metal of the azo metal complex shown in "5-3) anion portion: azo metal complex + cation portion: dye" is ion-bonded with two oxygen atoir.s, and thus, recording has been carried out by rotation between a U plane and a D plane produced by a ber.zene nucleus group. On the other hand, in the application example shown in FIGS. 110A, HOB, and HOC, the center metal is ion-bonded with four oxygen atoms, and ~hus, no rotation motion occurs. As in "5-5) azo metal complex in which center metal is ion-bonded with four oxygen atoms", recording is carried out based or. a difference in molecular arrangement. That is, as shown in FIG. 112A, before recording, molecule arrangement of an organic dye based recording material produced by combining the azo metal complex and the cyanine aye are provided. After recording, as shown in FIG. 1123, the molecular arrangement becomes random. As shown in FIG. 112A, in the case where molecules are arranged, a coagulation force acts, and as shown in FIG. 113, an

intermolecular distance in the cyanine dye is reduced. As a result, a wavelength of a maximum absorption wavelength A,bmax write before recording is shortened. In contrast, as shown in FIG. 112B, when random arrangement is provided, a coagulation force does not act, and an interatomic distance in the cyanine dye reverts to its original state. As a result, the wavelength of the maximum absorption wavelength ^amax writf ^s longer than A,bmax Write' anc* thereby "L-H" recording is carried out (refer to FIG. 106).
As shown in FIG. 112A, in the case of using a cyanine dye, the molecular size (molecular weight) of the cyanine dye is large, and thus, molecular arrangement is normally provided. However, as compared with FIG. 103A, arrangement stability is impaired, and random arrangement is likely to occur comparatively easily. Thus, in the case of using an organic dye based recording material having a structure shown in FIG. HOB, the stability of repetition reproduction is impaired. When repetition reproduction is carried out, there occurs a problem that molecular arrangement is randomized and data is destroyed. In contrast, in the case of using a combination of the azo metal complex and triethyl amine shown in FIG. 103A, the stability of normally provided molecular arrangement is very good, and a random structure is unlikely to occur. Thus, even if repetition reproduction is carried out,

recording data is not destroyed. In contrast, in a structure of the azo metal complex and triethyl amine shown in FIGS. 103A and 103B, random arrangement is unlikely to occur, and thus, no recording is carried out with low recording power. Therefore, there are provided rapid y-characteristics as shown in FIG. Ill (a) that, if recording power exceeds a certain threshold value, recording is suddenly carried cut.
In the structure shown in FIG. 103A, as shown in FIG. Ill (a), a gradient having y-characteristict; is steep, and is suitable for slice level detection. However, in the recording/reproducing apparatus according to the present embodiment, as shown in FIG. 13, a PRML detecting technique is used for reproduction, and thus, linearity is required for recording characteristics. In addition, in the cnaracteristics shown in FIG. Ill (a), the gradient of Y-characteristics is too steep, and no linearity-occurs, which is unsuitable for the PRML detecting technique. In contrast, in the case of an (anion/cation shaped) organic dye based recording material formed by combining the azo metal complex and cyanine dye shown in FIGS. 112A and 112B, Y-characteristics are gentle as shown in FIG. Ill (b), and the linearity for PRML detection is good. However, the stability of molecules at the time of arrangement is impaired, and random arrangement is likely to occur.

Thus, with reproduction power as well, a change in molecular arrangement occurs, lacking the stability of repetition reproduction. This application example is featured in that a recording layer is formed by mixing the organic dye based recording material having the characteristics shown in FIG. Ill (a) with the organic dye based recording material having the characteristics shown in FIG. Ill (b), thereby ensuring the linearity for PWML detection and ensuring the stability at the time of repetition reproduction. That is, a recording layer is formed by mixing an organic dye based recording material whose molecular weight is comparatively small shown in FIGS. 100A and 100B and an organic dye based recording material whose molecular weight is comparatively large shown in FIGS. 110A, HOB, and HOC. In the organic dye based recording material whose molecular weight is comparatively small shown in FIGS. 100A and 100B, the stability obtained when molecules are normally arranged is high as shown in FIGS. 103A and 103B, and the stability at the time of repetition reproduction can be ensured. In contrast, in the case of using the organic dye based recording material whose molecular weight is comparatively large shown in FIGS. 110A, HOB, and HOC, the stability at the time of normal molecular arrangement is impaired as shown in FIGS. 112A and 112B, and y-characteristics are gentle, and thus, the

linearity for PRML detection is good. In order to combine these organic dye based recording materials having their characteristics, it is desirable that a difference between molecular weights exceed 100. This is because the molecular weight of triethyl amine contained in FIGS. 100A and 100B is 118, and the molecular weight, of a cyanine dye shown in FIGS. 110A, HOB, and HOC is about 250, and thus, if a distance 100 or more occurs in molecular weight, organic dye based recording materials having different characteristics can be mixed with each other.
In addition, a plurality of mixed organic dye based recording materials each are featured in that each of these materials contains organic metal complex. In the present embodiment, an azo metal complex is used as an organic metal complex. A common organic metal complex is thus contained in the different organic dye based recording materials, and thereby the mixture stability obtained when both of them are mixed with each other can be enhanced. In addition, the present embodiment is featured in that a nitrogen-containing organic compound is used for an organic dye based recording material whose molecular weight is small, and an anion/cation is configured for an organic dye based recording material whose molecular weight is large from among a plurality of organic dye based recording materials. This is because, in the case of

anion/cation, both of the organic metal complex and dye have a coloring area, and thus, excellent light absorption characteristics and good recording characteristics can be ensured.
A recording layer is formed by mixing a plurality of organic dye based recording materials whose molecular weights are different from each other. A recording material having excellent recording characteristics is used for one organic dye based recording material and a recording material with good repetition reproducing characteristics is used for another organic dye based recording material. Then, these materials are mixed with each other, thereby making it possible to produce a recording layer which satisfies both of good recording characteristics and repetition reproducing characteristics.
FIG. 114 shows molecular arrangement at the time of an unrecorded mode when a recording layer has been formed by mixing an organic dye based recording material using "azo metal complex + tiethyl amine" and an organic dye based recording material using "azo metal complex + cyanine dye". In the present embodiment, a common organic metal complex (azo metal complex) is used in organic dye based recording materials which are different from each other, r.hus remarkably improving the stability of molecular arrangement when mixing is carried out as shown in

FIG. 114. In FIG. 114, since a coexisting ratio of "azo metal complex + triethyl amine" whose molecular weight is small is larger than that of "azo metal complex + cyanine dye" whose molecular weight is large, very stable molecular arrangement is produced, and random arrangement is unlikely to occur. This is because "azo metal complex + cyanine dye" is surrounded by a molecular group of "azo metal complex + triethyl amine" whose structure is comparatively stable. Thus, even if a temperature somewhat rises, there is provided a structure that "azo metal complex + cyanine dye" is blocked, and random molecular arrangement is unlikely to occur. In contrast, as shown in FIG. 115, if "azo metal complex + triethyl amine" whose molecular weight is small is lower in mixture ratio (ratio by weight) than "azo metal complex + cyanine dye" whose molecular weight is large, unnecessary gap areas 1002 and 1003 are produced, and thus, under the influence of these gap areas, molecular arrangement is likely to occur in random even at a slight temperature rise. As is evident from FIG. 114 and FIG. 115, in the case where a recording layer is formed by mixing a plurality of different dye based recording materials, molecular arrangement is stabilized and the degradation of signal characteristics at the time of repetition reproduction can be reduced by increasing a mixture ratio (ratio by weight) of organic dye based recording materials whose

molecular weight is small (increasing the ratio to 50% or more). Therefore, in the present embodiment, the mixture ratio of the organic dye based recording materials for the organic nitrogen compound whose molecular weight is small is larger than that of an anion/cation based organic dye based recording material whose molecular weight is large. When a recording layer is formed while changing the mixture ratic of the organic dye based recording materials whose molecular weights are different from each other, and recording characteristics and repetition reproducing stability are checked, it has been found that stability of molecular arrangement is enhanced when the mixture ratio of the organic dye recording materials whcse molecular weights are small is 1.5 times or more of that of the organic dye based recording materials whose molecular weights are large. In contrast, if the mixture ratio of the organic dye based recording materials whose molecular weights are small is significantly increased, the characteristics of the organic dye based recording materials whose molecular weights are large is lost. Thus, it has been found desirable that a ratio of the mixture ratio of the organic dye based recording materials whose molecular weights are small with respect to that of the organic dye based recording materials whose molecular weights are large is 8 times or less. In other words, a ratio

between the mixture ratio of the organic dye based recording materials whose molecular weights are small and that of the organic dye based recording materials whose molecular weights are large ranges from 1.5 : 1 to 8 : 1 (or alternatively, an organic dye based recording material whose molecular weight is small is included in 66% to 12.5%). Further, in order to ensure the linearity at the time of recording relative to detection in accordance with the PRML technique and to ensure the stability at the time of repetition reproduction, it has been found to be most desirable that the mixture ratio of the organic dye based recording materials whose molecular weights are small with respect to the organic dye based recording materials whose molecular weights are large ranges from 1.7 times to 3 times. FIGS. 108A and 108B has described that, when a polarized fluorine alcohol (tetra fluoro propanol) is used as an organic medium, molecules are arranged in random before recording and molecules are normally arranged after recording. Similar molecular arrangement can be produced as another application example of the above embodiment. That is, when a recording layer is formed while a plurality of organic dye based materials coexist, fluorine alcohol molecules partially remains in the recording layer, as shown in FIG. 116 if an organic medium (for example, fluorine alcohol) having

polarization property is used. In addition, as shown in FIG. 116, random molecular arrangement occurs in an unrecorded state, and the organic medium molecules volatilize at the time of recording. Thus, as shown in FIG. 114, molecules can be controlled to be arranged after recording.
FIG. Ill (c) shows characteristics in the case where an organic dye based recording material formed by combining the azo metal complex and triethyl amine shown in FIG. Ill (a) is merely combined with an (anion/cation type) organic dye based recording material formed by combining the azo metal complex and cyanine dye shown in FIG. Ill (b) in an equal mixture ratio. In this case, linearity is impaired, which is unsuitable for detection in accordance with the PRML technique. On the other hand, FIG. Ill (d) shows characteristic in the case where the organic dye based recording material formed by combining the azo metal complex and triethyl amine shown in FIG. Ill (a) is combined with the (anion/cation type) organic based recording material formed by the azo metal complex and cyanine dye shown in FIG. Ill (b) in a mixture ratio of about 6:4. According to the characteristics, linearity is good, which is suitable for detection in accordance with the PRML technique. In addition, a change in molecular arrangement is unlikely to occur with reproduction power, and the stability of repetition

reproduction can be ensured.
As described above, according to the present embodiment, it becomes possible to control characteristics of random property/regularities of molecular arrangement in a recording layer by combining organic dye based recording materials exceeding 100 in difference between molecular weights, and the recording characteristics and repetition reproducing characteristics can be easily changed.
In a plurality of organic dye based recording materials whose molecular weights are different from each other, it becomes possible to control characteristics of random property/regularities of molecular arrangement in the recording layer by including the same organic metal complex, and the recording characteristics and repetition reproduction characteristics can be easily changed.
In a plurality of organic dye based recording materials whose molecular weights are different from each other, at least one material configures anion/cation, and the structural stability in the recording layer can be ensured by including the nitrogen-containing organic compound in other ma t e r i a 1 s .
In the case of a structure in which two oxygen atoms are ion-bonded with the center metal shown in Chemical FIG. 3, a principle of recording is provided

by an arrangement angle between a U plane and a D plane produced by the benzene nucleus group, as shown in FIGS. 67A and 67B.
As described above, copper or the like is used as a material for the center metal M, and thereby molecular bonding is strengthened, and molecular destruction due to ultraviolet ray irradiation is unlikely to occur. Thus, the long-term stability is ensured as shown in FIGS. 67A and 67B. However, in the case where only two oxygen atoms are ion-bonded with the center metal M, as shown in FIGS. 67A and 67B, rotation easily occurs between the U plane and the D plane produced by the benzene nucleus group. Thus, by carrying out; repetition reproduction, an unrecorded area shown in FIG. 67A gradually changes to allocation after recording, as shown in FIG. 67B, and thus, there occurs a phenomenon that a recorded signal is degraded.
As an application example for solving the above-described problems, in the present embodiment, as shown in FIGS, 98A and 98B, there is employed a structure in which four oxygen atoms are ion-bonded with the center metal. In FIGS. 98A and 98B, cobalt Co having a trivalent ion is used as the center metal. According to this application example, without being limited thereto, ircn, rare earth metals, aluminum, yttrium or the ;ike car: be used as having trivalent center metal ions instead of cobalt. As described above, by using a

trivalent center metal ion, as shown in FIGS. 98A and 98B, ion bonding with four oxygen atoms can be achieved around the center metal ion. Four oxygen atoms are thus arranged at symmetrical positions at the periphery of the center metal cobalt ion, thereby inhibiting rotation on top and bottom faces under the influence of arrangement between the oxygen atoms. In this manner, recording data can be prevented from being erased by a rotational motion. FIGS. 98A and 98B show an azo metal complex as an example, an organic metal complex can be used without being limited thereto in the present embodiment. That is, the following embodiment can be carried out by using an organic metal complex having a structure in which trivalent center metal ions are ion-bonded with four oxygen atoms. In the structural formula shown in FIG. 98A, the coloring area 8 is composed of a connection portion between the benzene nucleus and nitrogen atom covalently bonded with each other. A specific three-dimensional structure is shown in FIG. 98B. The coloring areas 8 are allocated in the upper and lower planes, respectively, and are in a torsional relationship with each other. As shown in FIG. 98A, in the case where ion bonding with four oxygen atoms is achieved at the periphery of trivalent metal ions, one electron becomes excessive, and thus, a negative charge is provided at the periphery of the center metal. In the present embodiment, in order to

eliminate this negative charge, other polymers each having a positive charge is combined with each other. In the present embodiment, a nitrogen-containing organic compound is used as a polymer having a positive charge. As a specific material for the nitrogen-containing organic compound, in the present embodiment, there is employed triethyl amine whose structural formula is shown in FIG. 99A. A three-dimensional structural view is shown in FIG. 99B. While triethyl amine is used as a polymer having a positive charge in the present embodiment, without being limited thereto, there can be used in another embodiment: an aminium salt based compound; an amine compound; an amino ~hiol nickel complex based compound; an inmonium based compound; a cyanine based compound; an iminium based compound; a dithiol nickel complex compound; or cation such as an ammonium ion or a tetra alkyl ammonium ion. In addition, as the above amine compounds, there can be used: tripropyl amine; tributyl amine; secondary butyl amine; tertiary butyl amine; hexyl amine, N-methyl cyclohexyl amine; benzyl amine; N, N-diisopropyl ethyl amine; or 2, 6-xyidine and the like. Further, according to the present embodiment, a polymer having a positive charge is set to be equal to or smaller than a specific value of a molecular weight. Although the molecular weight of triethyl amine shown in FIG. 59A is 113, if the molecular weight of the polymer having a

positive charge exceeds 1200, the solubility relative to an organic solvent at the time of forming a recording layer is impaired, making it difficult to form a stable recording layer. Therefore, the molecular weight of this polymer having a positive charge is set to 1200 or less in the present embodiment. Further, from a variety of tests, ir has bee found desirable that a molecular weight is 250 or less as a condition that the solubility relative to a solvent is high.
In the present embodiment, an organic polymer is utilized as a substance having a positive change electrically neutralized with respect to an organic metal complex having a negative charge. In the present embodiment, a metal ion such as a sodium ion, for example, can be used without being limited thereto.
FIG. iOOA shows a three-dimensionally combined structural view formed by combining structural views of the azo metal complex shown in FIG. 98A and triethyl amine shown in FIG. 99A. Specifically, N+ in triethyl amine is allocated at a position proximal to the center metal cobalt, and the hydrogen atom proximal to zhe nitrogen ion in triethyl amine is partially inserted between cobalt and the coloring area 8. FIG. 1003 shows a schematic view relevant to a structural view shown in FIG. IOOA.
A description will be given below with respect to

a principle of coloring in the coloring area 8 in an azo metal complex shown in FIGS. 98A and 98B. FIG. 101A shows a part of the structural formula shown in FIG. 98A, and FIG. 101B shows a re-electron orbit at a portion which is covalently bonded in the structural formula. A re-electron orbit in the case where no center metal cobalt exists is indicated by dashed line. If a negative ion (cobalt atom having a charge) approaches the vicinity where electron orbits should be vertically and uniformly arranged essentially, the electron orbits are distorted, as shown in FIG. 101B, under the influence of the center metal ions. As a result, a coloring action is generated. While FIG. 101B describes an electron orbit at a repulsion caused by approaching of a negative charge for the sake of simplification, in actuality, a mixture orbit between a d-crbit which is part of metal atoms and the above re-orbit is produced, and coloring is carried out. In the re-electron distribution, as shown in FIG. 101C, the electron distribution density is the highest in the vicinity of atoms, and the electron distribution density is lev; between the atoms. This mixture orbit is featured as follows. That is, as shown in FIG. 102, when any force acts on an original interatomic distance, and then, the interatomic distance is reduced, the localization range of re-electrons becomes narrow as shown in FIG. 102 (a). As a result, a

wavelength of absorption light is shortened. In contrast, as shown in FIG. 102 (b), conversely, when the interatomic distance increases, the localization range of 7i-electrons becomes wide, and the wavelength of absorption light increases.
In the case of using the above-described organic dye based recording material, "change in intramolecular (inter-molecular) orientation and arrangement" is utilized in a principle of recording described in section "3-2-B] Basic characteristics common to organic dye recording materials in the present embodiment" in "3-2) Description of basic characteristics common to organic dye recording films in the present embodiment".
That is, in the case of using a combination of the azo metal complex and triethyl amine according to the present embodiment, combined molecules are normally arranged and allocated before recording. As a result, as shown in FIG. 103A, a coagulation force 1001 acts in a vertical direction. In addition, at the time of recording, the arrangement of molecules greatly moves under the influence of thermal energy, and, after recording, the molecules are arranged in random as shown in FIG. 103B. As a result, the coagulation force weakens as compared with FIG. 103A. In addition, as shown in FIG. 98B, four oxygen atoms ion-bonded with the center metal are bonded with one carbon atom

contained in the benzene nucleus in the coloring area 8. Thus, as shown in FIG. 103A, if a coagulation force 1001 acts, the oxygen atoms push up the benzene nucleus. As shown in FIG. 104, an interatomic distance increases at the periphery of the carbon atom bonded with the pushed up oxygen atoms. Conversely, an interatomic distance between the carbon atoms is reduced in the benzene nucleus situated at a position distant from the oxygen atoms. As a result, the range of absorption light widens, and the width of light absorption spectra increases (refer to FIG. 106 "half value width Was before recording").
Further, as shown in FIG. 99B, three carbon atoms. and one hydrogen atom surrounding nitrogen ions contained in triethyl amine have a regular tetrahedron structure, and are formed in a wedge shape relative to the azo metal complex. Thus, the coagulation force acts, and thereby, as shown in FIG. 105, triethyl amine pushes out the nitrogen atom or carbon atom from the inside of the coloring area 8. As a result, a distance between carbon atoms, a distance between a nitrogen atom and a carbon atom, or a distance between nitrogen atoms is reduced, and the maximum absorption wavelength ^-brnax writ^ is reduced. As a result, as shown in FIG. 106 (bN, the half value width Was of the absorption spectra before recording is wide, and the value of the maximum absorption wavelength Xbmax write

is short. On the other hand, as shown in FIG. 103B, if a coagulation force weakens by allocation of molecules in random after recording, the above-described pushing force weakens. As a result, interatomic distances return to their original state. Thus, as shown in FIG. 106A, the maximum absorption wavelength ^amax write is shifted to the long wavelength side as compared with A,bmax Write' an^ tne half value width Was is narrowed. As a result, light absorbance decreases from A14Q5 to Ah4Q5 at a position of a reproduction light beam of 405 nm in wavelength, and a light reflectivity increases. As has been described above, the present embodiment is featured in that an organic dye based recording material is configured by a combination of an organic metal complex and a nitrogen-containing organic compound, wherein a trivalent center metal ion and four oxygen atoms are ion-bonded with each other, and as shown in FIGS. 103A and 103B, recording is carried out by a change in inter-molecular arrangement, thereby having "L-H" recording characteristics.
As has been described previously, in the case where a intra-molecular (or inter-molecular orientation cr arrangement change)" occurs, a change rate in maximum absorption wavelength caused by a change in interatomic distance is comparatively small. Thus, as described in Formulas (50) and (51) above, a value of

the maximum absorption wavelength change is small, and thus, a characteristic dispersion between mediums before and after recording can be reduced when a large number of write-once type information storage mediums 12 has been mass-produced; and the performance stability at the time of mass-production can be ensured. Therefore, in the present embodiment, a contrivance is made so as to meet a condition of AXrnax Another application example relevant to a principle of recording shown in FIGS. 103A and 1033 will be described below.
In FIGS. 103A and 103B, molecules are normally arranged in order before recording, and are arranged in random after recording. However, in another application example shown below, conversely, a principle of recording is provided such that molecules are arranged in random before recording, and are arranged in order after recording. In order to enable this principle of recording, the present embodiment is featured in that a solvent having polarity is utilized when a recording layer using an organic dye based recording material is formed. As a specific solvent having polarity, fluorine alcohol is used in the present embodiment. As an example of fluorine alcohol,

FIG. 107A shows a structural formula of tetra fluoro propanol (TFP).
As shown in FIG. 107A, in tetra fluoro propanol, three carbon atoms are produced a main chain, and fluorine atoms are arranged at the periphery thereof, and an OH group is arranged at a terminal. Here, electron eccentricity occurs between the OH group and the carbon atoms adjacent thereto, and, as shown in FIG. 107A, negatively charged polarization occurs at the OH group side, and positively charged polarization occurs at the carbon side adjacent thereto. In this case, the schematic view is shown in FIG. 107B. The molecules of the azo metal complex and triethyl amine having a structure shown in FIG. 100B are dissolved in a tetra fluoro propanol solvent shown in FIG. 107A, and is coated onto a transparent substrate, thereby forming a recording layer. At this time, tetra fluoro propanol has polarization, and a portion at which the center metal (cobalt) in the azo metal complex and nitrogen ions in triethyl amine are arranged and the tetra fluoro propanol are attracted toward each other. As a result, there occurs a phenomenon that tetra fluoro propanol which is an organic solvent partially remains immediately after forming the recording layer. As a result, the remaining tetra fluoro propanol without being volatilized inhibits provision of molecular arrangement. Then, as shown in FIG. 108A, organic dye

molecules are arranged in random. In FIG. 108A, there are shown tetra fluoro propanol molecules when a portion expressed in the schematic view of FIG. 107B remains without being volatilized. At the time of recording, a high temperature occurs, the remaining organic solvent molecules completely volatilize, and thus, a factor which inhibits arrangement is dissolved. As a result, after recording, organic dye molecules are arranged each other as shown in FIG. 108B. Now, a description will be given with respect to effect of molecular arrangement on a reproduction signal in FIGS. 108A and 108B.
As shown in FIG. 108A, at a portion at which tetra fluoro propanol which is an organic solvent molecule remains, under its influence, there increases a distance between cobalt in the azo metal complex and a nitrogen ion in triethyl amine. Then, as shown in FIG. 109A, an effect caused by only a cobalt ion appears with respect to covalent bonding in the coloring area 8. In contrast, when an organic solvent molecule having polarization volatilizes, the nitrogen ion in triethyl amine approaches the center metal in the azo metal complex (FIG. 109B). Thus, charge based neutralization occurs due to a charge of the nitrogen ion, and a rr-electron orbit extends downwardly as shown in FIG. 109C. In this manner, the maximum absorption wavelength increases. As a result, as shown in

FIG. 106, Xamax write is greater than Xbmax write/ and the light absorbance changes from A1405 to An405 wnen reproduction is carried out with a reproduction light beam of 405 nm in wavelength, and such a change appears as a reproduction signal. However, as shown in FIGS. 109A, 109B, and 109C, a change rate of a n-electron orbit due to charge based neutralization of nitrogen ions is very small, and thus, a wavelength difference AXmax between Xamax write and *-bmax write shown in FIG. 106 is small, and the formula (50) or formula (51) described above is met. Thus, a specific dispersion between mediums before and after recording is reduced, and stable mass-production can be achieved when a large number of write-once type information recording mediums 12 have been mass-produced. Chapter 6: Description Relating to Pre-groove shape/pre-pit shape in coating type organic dye recording film and on light reflection layer interface
6-1) Light reflection layer
As described in "Chapter 0: Description of Relationship between Use Wavelength and the Present Embodiment", the present embodiment assumes a range of 355 nm to 455 nm in particular around 405 nm. When the metal materials each having a high light reflection factor at this wavelength bandwidth are arranged in order from the highest light reflection factor, Ag is in the order of around 96%; Al is in the order of around 80%, and Rh is in the order of around 80%. In a write-one type information storage medium using an organic dye recording material, as shown in FIG. 2B, the reflection light from the light reflection layer 4-2 is a standard, and thus, the light reflection layer 4-2 requires a high light reflection factor in characteristics. In particular, in the case of the "H-L" recording film according to the present embodiment, the light reflection factor in an unrecorded area is low. Thus, if the light reflection factor in the light reflection layer 4-2 simplex is low, in particular, a reproduction signal C/N rario from a pre-pit (emboss) area is low, lacking the stability at the time of reproduction. Thus, in particular, it is mandatory that the light reflection

factor in the light reflection layer 4-2 simplex is high. Therefore, in the present embodiment, in the above wavelength bandwidth, a material mainly made of Ag (silver) having the highest reflection factor is used. As a material for the light reflection layer 4-2, there occurs a problem that "atoms easily move" or "corrosion easily occurs" if silver is used alone. To solve the first problem, when partial alloying is carried out by adding other atoms, silver atoms hardly move. In the first embodiment in which other atoms are added, the light reflection layer 4-2 is made of AgNdCu according to the first embodiment. AgNdCu is in a solid soluble state, and thus, the reflection factor is slightly lowered than a state in which silver is used alone. In the second embodiment in which other atoms are added, the light reflection layer 4-2 is made of AgPd, and an electric potential is changed, whereby corrosion hardly occurs in an electrochemical manner. If the light reflection layer 4-2 corrodes due tc silver oxidization or the like, the light reflection factor is lowered. In an organic dye recording film having a recording film structure shown in FIG. 2B, in particular, in the case of an organic dye recording film shown in "Chapter 3: Description of Characteristics of Organic Dye Recording Film in the Present Embodiment", in particular, a light reflection factor on an interface between the recording layer 3-2

and the light reflection later 4-2 is very important. If correction occurs on this interface, the light reflection factor is lowered, and an optical interface shape blurs. In addition, the detection signal characteristics from a track shift detection signal (push-pull signal) or a wobble signal and a pre-pit (emboss) area are degraded. In addition, in the case where the width Wg of the pre-groove area 11 is v.-ider than the width Wl of the land area, a track shift detection signal (push-pull signal) or a wobble signal is hardly generated, thus increasing effect of degradation of the light reflection factor on the interface between the recording layer 3-2 and the light reflection layer 4-2 due to corrosion. In order to prevent degradation of the light reflection factor on this interface, AgBi is used for the light reflection layer 4-2 as the third embodiment. AgBi forms a very stable phase and prevents degradation of the light reflection factor on the above interface because a passive coat film is formed on a surface (interface between the recording layer 3-2 and the light reflection layer 4-2). That is, if Bi (bismuth) is slightly added to Ag, Bi is isolated from the above interface, the isolated Bi is oxidized. Then, a very fine film (passive coat film) called oxidized bismuth is formed to function to preclude internal oxidization. This passive coat film is formed on the interface, and

forms a very stable phase. Thus, the degradation of a light reflection factor does not occur, and the stability of detection signal characteristics from a track shift detection signal (push-pull signal) or a wobble signal and a pre-pit (emboss) area is guaranteed over a long period of time. At a wavelength band ranging from 355 nm to 455 nm, the silver simplex has the highest light reflection factor, and the light reflection factor is lowered as an additive amount of other atoms is increased. Thus, it is desirable that an additive amount of Bi atoms in AgBi in the present embodiment be equal to or smaller than 5at%. The unit of at-a used here denotes atomic percent, and indicates that five Bi atoms exist in a total atom number 100 of AgBi., for example. When characteristics have been evaluated by actually producing the passive coat film, it has found that a passive coat film can be produced as long as an additive amount of Bi atoms is equal to or greater than 0.5at%. Based on a result of chis evaluation, an additive amount of Bi atoms in "he light reflection layer 4-2 in the present embodiment is defined as lat%. In this third embodiment, only one atom Bi is added, and an additive amount of atoms can be reduced as compared with AgNdCu according to the first embodiment (a case in which two types of atoms Nd and Cu is added in Ag), and AgBi can increase ~he light reflection factor more significantly than AgNdCu. As a

result, even in the case of the "H-L" recording film according to the present embodiment or in the case where the width Wg of the pre-groove area 11 is wider than the with Wl of the land area, as shown in FIGS. 8B and 8C, a detection signal can be stably obtained from a track shift detection signal (push-pull signal) or a wobble signal and a pre-pit (emboss) area with high precision. The third embodiment is not limited to AgBi, and a ternary system including AgMg, AgNi, AgGa, AgNx, AgCo, AgAl or the atoms described previously may be used as a silver allow which produces a passive coat film. The thickness of this light reflection layer 4-2 is set in the range of 5 nm to 200 nm. If the thickness is smaller than 5 nm, the light reflection layer 4-2 is not uniform, and is formed in a land shape. Therefore, the thickness of the light reflection layer 4-2 is set to 5 nm. When an AgBi film is equal to or smaller than 80 nm in thickness, the film permeates to its back side. Thus, in the case of a one-sided single recording layer, the thickness is set in the range of 80 nm to 200 nm, and preferably, in the range of 100 nm to 150 nm. In the case of a onesided double recording layer, the thickness is set in the range of 5 nm to 15 nm.
